<div id="review_2756204552" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2756204552" />
    <a title="Forrest" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/811928-forrest"><img alt="Forrest" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1558621304p2/811928.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2756204552?book_show_action=true">Apr 04, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Forrest" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Forrest" href="/user/show/811928-forrest">Forrest</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780451013897" href="/book/show/6474002-the-stars-my-destination">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2756204552" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15747276188793492559">Stamped on the inside front cover of this used book is the following:<br/><br/>William Howell<br/><a href='https://www.mapquest.com/search/result?query=620%20N.%20Oakhill%20Janesville,%20WI&boundingBox=43.05973257416383,-89.37013149261473,43.03812464542969,-89.31906223297119&page=0&index=0' rel='nofollow noopener'>620 N. Oakhill<br/>Janesville, WI</a><br/>PLEASANT 2-0543<br/>MAY--1961<br/><br/>Who was this? He owned and likely read this book 8 years before I was born. He might be older than my father, if he's still alive. Is he? My daughter and grandson live in Janesville. Do they ever walk past that address? Does he still live there? Is any of this relevant to the book? Maybe . . . maybe . . . in the end. But I’m not giving away the end. No, you need </span>
  <span id="freeText15747276188793492559" style="display:none">Stamped on the inside front cover of this used book is the following:<br /><br />William Howell<br /><a href="https://www.mapquest.com/search/result?query=620%20N.%20Oakhill%20Janesville,%20WI&amp;boundingBox=43.05973257416383,-89.37013149261473,43.03812464542969,-89.31906223297119&amp;page=0&amp;index=0" rel="nofollow noopener">620 N. Oakhill<br />Janesville, WI</a><br />PLEASANT 2-0543<br />MAY--1961<br /><br />Who was this? He owned and likely read this book 8 years before I was born. He might be older than my father, if he's still alive. Is he? My daughter and grandson live in Janesville. Do they ever walk past that address? Does he still live there? Is any of this relevant to the book? Maybe . . . maybe . . . in the end. But I’m not giving away the end. No, you need to work for it.<br /><br />I suppose the mystery engendered by this name and address put me in the proper frame of mind to explore the personality of Gulliver Foyle, the anti-hero of the book. Gully is driven by vengeance, driven by himself – and I mean this in a very literal, physical sense. But you won’t know why I mean that until the end. Like William Howell, he is an enigma. Even an enigma to himself, which we grow to learn as we explore the interstices of Foyle’s near-animal brain.<br /><br />This book must be read straight through. Don’t set it aside. This book is . . . sudden. It takes sudden, unexpected turns. Yes, it starts out with an infodump. And normally I hate infodumps. But this one is critical to the story. When you get to the end . . . again, don’t stop till you get there . . . you will see how the infodump at the beginning was totally necessary to the success of the entire story. Bester has ensured that all the necessary loose ends are tied up. “Necessary,” because there are plenty of loose ends left at the end. But they make sense, in the context of the story. This is a tight biome for your brain, but it leaves room for . . . “growth” is the word that comes to mind.<br /><br />Now, you might want to cheat and head straight to the end and read it. But I guarantee the story will make no sense whatsoever to you if you do that. This is as much an experience as it is a piece of writing. It envelops the reader’s brain while the reader’s brain simultaneously envelops it. It’s as close as one can get to some of the deeper mysteries of quantum mechanics by merely reading words on a page. And it causes the reader to reflect on their own inner being, a sort of science-fiction Rorshach test.<br /><br />It took me by surprise. Though I had heard for many years just how “good” it was, I don’t think that any words (other than the words of the book itself) can convey the way that Bester grabs the attention of the reader and immerses them in the tale. As one finally starts to come up for water, one realizes just how deeply enmeshed they are in the story. Love or hate him, we are all, in some way, Gully Foyle.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="15747276188793492559" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1527911249" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1527911249" />
    <a title="Scott" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/36819318-scott"><img alt="Scott" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1485843897p2/36819318.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1527911249?book_show_action=true">Jan 27, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Scott" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Scott" href="/user/show/36819318-scott">Scott</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36819318-scott?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1527911249" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3110317664737462392">I <i>love</i> the thrill of discovering an older work of SF that still rocks. <br/><br/><i>The Stars My Destination</i> is one such book, a thrill ride from beginning to end that despite being published in 1955 still hits hard and holds its own in 2017. <br/><br/>Several times while reading <i>The Stars My Destination</i> a very clear thought occurred to me- this <i>shouldn't</i> be working. The narrative is flush with odd plot developments, amusing 1950s sci-fi anachronisms (Newspapers being printed in the far future when they're struggling </span>
  <span id="freeText3110317664737462392" style="display:none">I <i>love</i> the thrill of discovering an older work of SF that still rocks. <br /><br /><i>The Stars My Destination</i> is one such book, a thrill ride from beginning to end that despite being published in 1955 still hits hard and holds its own in 2017. <br /><br />Several times while reading <i>The Stars My Destination</i> a very clear thought occurred to me- this <i>shouldn't</i> be working. The narrative is flush with odd plot developments, amusing 1950s sci-fi anachronisms (Newspapers being printed in the far future when they're struggling for readers in 2017) non-sequitur story twists (to my mind) and a foundation premise - scientists discover everyone innately has the power to teleport themselves - that is pretty thin. Yet despite all this I really dug Bester's novel, and I raced through it. <br /><br />From the first few pages, where Bester's main character Gully Foyle is trapped for months in a psyche-warpingly small closet (the only sealed compartment left in his crippled ship) and eventually plans his rather gripping escape I was hooked. Foyle goes from zero-to-homicidally-driven-anti-hero over the course of a chapter and what happens to him in the wreckage of his vessel sets him off on a novel-length quest for revenge against the people who abandoned him.<br /><br />The book runs at a sweat-inducing pace, dashing from development to development and only rarely stopping to catch its breath. Things happen. They happen fast and they happen big, and as the story progresses Foyle's transformation from listless bottom-of-the-heap loser to implacable, resourceful hunter and beyond is very satisfying. <br /><br />Some golden age SF can't transcend the period in which it was written, and is mired in concepts that are now outdated, or modes of storytelling that present day readers can find dull (see some of Asimov's short stories for prime examples of this type.) <br /><br /><i>The Stars My Destination</i> in contrast, is still fresh. Its flaws are minor and its storytelling is both straightforward and engaging.<br /><br />In short, it's well worth your time. I rate the pulse-quickening opening sequence in the crippled ship as being right up there with the best parts of <i>The Martian</i> and I rank this novel as one of the classics of its era.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3110317664737462392" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_581269893" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/581269893" />
    <a title="Stuart" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9456990-stuart"><img alt="Stuart" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1452041473p2/9456990.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/581269893?book_show_action=true">Apr 04, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Stuart" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Stuart" href="/user/show/9456990-stuart">Stuart</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780575094192" href="/book/show/8493755-the-stars-my-destination">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9456990-stuart?shelf=classic-sf">classic-sf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9456990-stuart?shelf=galaxy-spanning">galaxy-spanning</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9456990-stuart?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer581269893" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9024417779001743882">The Stars My Destination: Tiger, Tiger, Burning Bright, Intent on Revenge<br/>(Posted at <a href='http://www.fantasyliterature.com/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Fantasy Literature</a>)<br/>Much has been written about Alfred Bester’s classic 1956 SF novel The Stars My Destination (Tiger! Tiger! in the UK edition). According to Wikipedia, it is considered one of the best SF books of all time by many authors such as Neil Gaiman, Joe Haldeman, Samuel. R. Delany, Robert Silverberg, and William Gibson. Predating cyberpunk by almost three decades (if you count from Neuromancer in 1984),</span>
  <span id="freeText9024417779001743882" style="display:none">The Stars My Destination: Tiger, Tiger, Burning Bright, Intent on Revenge<br />(Posted at <a href="http://www.fantasyliterature.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Fantasy Literature</a>)<br />Much has been written about Alfred Bester’s classic 1956 SF novel The Stars My Destination (Tiger! Tiger! in the UK edition). According to Wikipedia, it is considered one of the best SF books of all time by many authors such as Neil Gaiman, Joe Haldeman, Samuel. R. Delany, Robert Silverberg, and William Gibson. Predating cyberpunk by almost three decades (if you count from Neuromancer in 1984), it features a fully-realized world of ruthless multinational corporations, cybernetic enhancements, and most importantly, the concept of “jaunting”, the ability to teleport instantly between two places if the jaunter knows the exact locations and has seen them before physically. This ability is available to almost everyone in society. As you might expect, this created dramatic upheaval in global society and has completely transformed economies, transportation, and social behavior. For instance, due to the ability of people to jaunt into any known location, wealthy families create impenetrable labyrinths to protect themselves and women are confined to such places in many cases, giving rise to a Neo-Victorian society. <br /><br />The story begins in very cinematic fashion with a lone crewman named Gully Foyle, who wakes up to find himself the sole survivor of an attack on a merchant spaceship called Nomad. He initially finds ways to survive but is not pushed into action until a passing ship, the Vorga, ignores the distress signals he has been sending out. This fuels an intense rage in him that will consume and transform him utterly into a single-minded beast driven by the desire for revenge on whomever controlled the Vorga. As it turns out, the Vorga is owned by the same ultra-wealthy and decadent Presteign clan that owns the Nomad, and the further Gully pursues each link in the mystery behind the Vorga’s actions, the more convoluted the plot becomes, and he encounters a plethora of very unusual and intriguing characters. Along the way, he himself changes in dramatic ways and we also get a very detailed tour of this future world where teleportation dominates. There are even some telepaths (echoes of Bester’s previous novel The Demolished Man, which won the inaugural Hugo Award) in the story, a mysterious super-powerful substance called PyrE, a “jaunt-proof” high security prison, a primitive space-bound cargo cult, various assassins and secret societies, and a struggle between the Inner Planets and Outer Colonies, which is a theme that has been explored in the genre many times since, including most recently James S.A. Corey’s THE EXPANSE series. <br /><br />Perhaps the biggest question for modern readers is, does this classic still hold up today, almost 60 years after initial publication? The answer is ABSOLUTELY! This book is fierce, cynical, lighting-paced, complex, philosophical, darkly humorous, and frankly doesn’t feel dated at all. It’s more exciting as cyberpunk than William Gibson, not as self-congratulatory as Iain M. Banks’ Culture novels, and takes a far more skeptical of the future than Robert Heinlein’s SF novels. Stylistically, it runs circles around the pedestrian prose of contemporaries like Arthur C. Clarke (who I like) or Isaac Asimov (who I don’t). Considering how much impact Bester has had on the genre with only two major books, The Demolished Man and The Stars My Destination, I think every serious SF fan owes it to themself to give this book a try.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9024417779001743882" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

<div id="review_5236025" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/5236025?book_show_action=true">Aug 28, 2007</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Adam" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Adam" href="/user/show/214053-adam">Adam</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">People who wonder what &quot;classic&quot; means</span></div>

        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer5236025" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer273648738685957766">Fast and furious and blackly comedic similiar to early Vonnegut or Jack Vance mixed with the bitter surrealism of Finney's "Circus of Doctor Lao", this book predicted and influenced trends like the British New Wave,cyberpunk, and new space opera, but retains an oddball flavor of its own. Satirizing 50's anxieties like the red scare and the threat of nuclear annihilation(and unhindered corporate greed and warmongering)and featuring a psychopathic protagonist(loose in world that makes him look lik</span>
  <span id="freeText273648738685957766" style="display:none">Fast and furious and blackly comedic similiar to early Vonnegut or Jack Vance mixed with the bitter surrealism of Finney's "Circus of Doctor Lao", this book predicted and influenced trends like the British New Wave,cyberpunk, and new space opera, but retains an oddball flavor of its own. Satirizing 50's anxieties like the red scare and the threat of nuclear annihilation(and unhindered corporate greed and warmongering)and featuring a psychopathic protagonist(loose in world that makes him look like a boyscout) this book has barely dated a day since its writing, especially since everything it satirizes has not left us. Add a truly satisfying conclusion and explanation of the economic impact of teleportation makes this book truly classic.</span>
  <a data-text-id="273648738685957766" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_59689054" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/59689054" />
    <a title="Felina" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/852687-felina"><img alt="Felina" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1559188448p2/852687.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/59689054?book_show_action=true">Jun 14, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Felina" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Felina" href="/user/show/852687-felina">Felina</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/852687-felina?shelf=star-2">star-2</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/852687-felina?shelf=2012">2012</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer59689054" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6531953175393760085"><i>Gully Foyle is my name<br/>And Terra is my nation.<br/>Deep space is my dwelling place,<br/>The stars my destination.</i><br/><br/><i>A man is a member of society first, and an individual second. You must go along with society, whether it chooses destruction or not.</i><br/><br/>Here's the break down:<br/><br/>Characterization - What a book of incredibly unlikable people. All the female characters are happy to be victims and while they are pretty badass in some regards are totally obsessed with love. Ummm...shut up. All the male characters are power </span>
  <span id="freeText6531953175393760085" style="display:none"><i>Gully Foyle is my name<br />And Terra is my nation.<br />Deep space is my dwelling place,<br />The stars my destination.</i><br /><br /><i>A man is a member of society first, and an individual second. You must go along with society, whether it chooses destruction or not.</i><br /><br />Here's the break down:<br /><br />Characterization - What a book of incredibly unlikable people. All the female characters are happy to be victims and while they are pretty badass in some regards are totally obsessed with love. Ummm...shut up. All the male characters are power hungry assholes. Not a hero or friend in the lot. The main character, of course, is supposed to be horrible...rapist, sociopath, psychopath, you name it. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Its kind of worse once you find out he is locked in a prison of his own making. I think Bester meant to make that some kind of redemption for the character but it kind of made it worse  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. But as I don't think the author intended for me to like any of the characters (at least not until the end) I can't really fault him on that front but I will say that it's odd to cast a bunch of douche bags.<br /><br />Story - The central plot is fairly entertaining. It takes a little to long to wrap up and there are far to many tangents that are not fully realized. The book should have been shorter and some of these tangents edited out or it should have been longer with the tangents fleshed out. Either way not quite there.<br /><br />Concept/story line - Kind of brilliant. There was a really good idea in here. Sometimes it was hard to see. This concept is something I think Asimov would have been better equipped to convey. The story is pretty heady and eventually ends up in a really fascinating place. A really good tale about good and evil and what makes a person good or evil. <br /><br />World Building - Excellent. I liked the description of the different races/planets. I liked how society was described (i.e. the different 'houses' dressing according to the year their ancestors changed history). I loved everything that happened in Gouffre Martel. I would have liked the outlawing of religions to be discussed a little more. There were hints in conversations about things that I would have preferred to have read about over Gully's story like WWIII. And, of course, jaunting was a great idea. Brilliant actually. What happens at the end with Gully <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[and the jaunting through space/time was amazing. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> I didn't see that coming at all it and opened the book up quite a bit.<br /><br />Tropes/Cliches - Way to much love at first sight bull shit. I hate that crap. I want to understand why people are into each other. If its just physical fine... I can understand that but these characters are all so flimsy. As soon as the relationships form you can actually see the respect for the woman disappear. When a female character would offer advice it was listened to but once a female character became someones 'property' they would get ignored. There is one section where a female character is talking to Gully and she makes a point of telling him she is now Mrs. whatever. It had no bearing on the story, the scene or the character development. But this was written in the 50's so I guess thats to be expected.<br /><br />Bester has a knack for action writing and physical description. That is probably the best part of this book. Its not terribly long. Just 258 pages. The story is interesting enough to stick with. At about 200 pages in I could have easily quit reading it and been fine with it. It was the last 50 pages that made the difference. It was in the last 50 pages that had the best dialogue, the best story line, the best character development and the best writing. Bester designed this book to come together at the end but unfortunately failed to make the reader realize that would happen, so throughout the entire book I'm searching for connections and coming up empty and blaming myself for missing the point. I don't like that. A lot of stories are like that but not all of those stories make you feel like its totally over your head. I had this pegged for a 3 star but I'm pushing it down to 2 stars.<br /><br />I'm still not sure what the plan was with the cast of idiots and assholes though.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6531953175393760085" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2025193555" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2025193555" />
    <a title="Lindsay" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10326608-lindsay"><img alt="Lindsay" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1588746288p2/10326608.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2025193555?book_show_action=true">Jun 10, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lindsay" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lindsay" href="/user/show/10326608-lindsay">Lindsay</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2025193555" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7612052618175355447">A pioneering work of science fiction that captures the dreams and fears of its time while maintaining an entertaining and madcap story.<br/><br/>Gully Foyle is marooned in space in the wreckage of a spaceship. After six months of barely surviving another spaceship approaches, clearly sees him and then <i>leaves him to die</i>. Gully is a low-class uninspired person, but this event catalyzes his monumental will to live and focuses it into a psychopathic lust for revenge where mere survival takes a distant seconda</span>
  <span id="freeText7612052618175355447" style="display:none">A pioneering work of science fiction that captures the dreams and fears of its time while maintaining an entertaining and madcap story.<br /><br />Gully Foyle is marooned in space in the wreckage of a spaceship. After six months of barely surviving another spaceship approaches, clearly sees him and then <i>leaves him to die</i>. Gully is a low-class uninspired person, but this event catalyzes his monumental will to live and focuses it into a psychopathic lust for revenge where mere survival takes a distant secondary role. Through a series of adventures Gully reinvents himself through education and accomplishment, always drawing closer to the revenge he seeks and almost always defeated by his own psychopathic compulsions.<br /><br />There are elements of the 1950s all through this work, from the simmering cold war between the Inner Planets and the Outer Satellites, to the imminent apocalyptic destructive potential of the PyrE substance that much of the plot revolves around, to the rise of corporate conformity culture that we see with the Mr Prestos of the Presteign company. There's also a sign of the Campbellian SF times with a large part of the plot concerning mental powers of teleportation (Jaunting) and telepathy.<br /><br />It's also very clear how influential this book was on later works. The sheer insanity of the Fourmyle Circus seems to me a clear antecedent of Zelazny's <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13821.Lord_of_Light" title="Lord of Light by Roger Zelazny" rel="nofollow noopener">Lord of Light</a> and other writers of the New Wave.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7612052618175355447" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1735112344" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1735112344" />
    <a title="Jim" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/695116-jim"><img alt="Jim" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1340192527p2/695116.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1735112344?book_show_action=true">Aug 21, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jim" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jim" href="/user/show/695116-jim">Jim</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audio Cassette " href="/book/show/20839354-the-stars-my-destination">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/695116-jim?shelf=scifi">scifi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/695116-jim?shelf=2fiction">2fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/695116-jim?shelf=1audio">1audio</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1735112344" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12290763396774870770">4 stars is a bit of stretch for a space opera with plot holes I could pilot a ship through, but I allowed for when it was written, the ideas contained, & the narration. As a straight SF novel today, it's barely OK - the characters are unlikable, the science magical, & the romance is ridiculous - yet it manages to leverage these weaknesses into a story that is really intriguing & even inspiring, if you can put your sense of disbelief on hold. <br/><br/>Gully Foyle, the MC, certainly isn't a hero. He's a be</span>
  <span id="freeText12290763396774870770" style="display:none">4 stars is a bit of stretch for a space opera with plot holes I could pilot a ship through, but I allowed for when it was written, the ideas contained, &amp; the narration. As a straight SF novel today, it's barely OK - the characters are unlikable, the science magical, &amp; the romance is ridiculous - yet it manages to leverage these weaknesses into a story that is really intriguing &amp; even inspiring, if you can put your sense of disbelief on hold. <br /><br />Gully Foyle, the MC, certainly isn't a hero. He's a beast that slowly becomes not just human, but the epitome of humanity in many ways. His crude, bestial drive leads him to break long established boundaries &amp; eventually inspire all of humanity in a devil's deal delivered in the low class argot of the time. <br /><i>"Take a war to make you spend. Take a jam to make you think. Take a challenge to make you great. Rest of the time you sit around lazy, you. Pigs, you! All right, God damn you! I challenge you, me. Die or live and be great. Bow yourselves to Christ gone or come and find me, Gully Foyle, and I make you men. I make you great. I give you the stars."</i><br />Fantastic. <br /><br />The neat ideas:<br />- Synesthesia was known back then, but I've read this was one of the earliest popular novels that used it.<br />- One of the early, best examples of modern cybernetics. Not just as a prosthetic, but as augmentation.<br />- Time/space/dimensions as parts of a whole.<br />- Religion outlawed &amp; become a 'filthy practice', yet people still use its words for profanity. Not explored enough, though.<br />- The drug 'analogue', not explored enough, but really intriguing.<br />- What psi powers would do to people &amp; society. The main power is that most can teleport, but telepathy was also used to great advantage.<br />There were more. Many weren't explored well enough, but created the impression of a real world, drawn with broad, exacting strokes that teased.<br /><br />Many of the things I disliked about the novel were also strengths. For instance, Olivia, the pampered daughter of one of the richest, most amoral men on Earth, is 'blind', yet she's not. She simply sees in a different spectrum than the rest &amp; her character makes absolutely no sense. In one scene she sees things no one else can &amp; revels in her power, yet in another she uses this as a reason for hating humanity. The dated treatment of the female characters doesn't help, but her sight was really unique, interesting, &amp; disappointing.<br /><br />The elite families of the Earth were ludicrous &amp; dated, but fun both for the way they were caricatured &amp; for the names themselves. While most were recognizable today, I doubt many today would recognize Esso, once a household name, but immersed since the 70s in the Exxon brand. Anyway, it was kind of a blast from the past.<br /><br />I think I read this way back when, but had forgotten most of it. I recently stumbled across a list in my documents "The Top 100 Audio Science Fiction Books". There are actually only 99 on the list &amp; one of those is a duplicate, so it's not to be taken too seriously. Still, it was enough to spur me to listening to this &amp; I'm glad I did. It's not a long book &amp; one of the foundations of SF. It's worth reading, but don't go into it expecting modern SF. It has warts, but should be treasured for them.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12290763396774870770" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_51859349" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/51859349" />
    <a title="Bill" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1811095-bill"><img alt="Bill" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1230361156p2/1811095.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/51859349?book_show_action=true">Apr 07, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bill" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bill" href="/user/show/1811095-bill">Bill</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780575094192" href="/book/show/8493755-the-stars-my-destination">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1811095-bill?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1811095-bill?shelf=2011">2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1811095-bill?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1811095-bill?shelf=sf-fantasy">sf-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1811095-bill?shelf=library-book">library-book</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer51859349" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17472495490900707050">when i was much younger, in my teens and early to mid twenties, i read a lot of sf.it was fun, it was exciting and full of adventure. then when i got into my later twenties, i pretty much lost interest. i'd read a lot of the classic stuff, a lot of the authors i liked were either retired or dead, and fantasy was taking over from science fiction with books about dragons and wizards and their ilk, and that really didn't turn me on.<br/><br/>so then, for close to 30 years, i read very little sf at all and i </span>
  <span id="freeText17472495490900707050" style="display:none">when i was much younger, in my teens and early to mid twenties, i read a lot of sf.it was fun, it was exciting and full of adventure. then when i got into my later twenties, i pretty much lost interest. i'd read a lot of the classic stuff, a lot of the authors i liked were either retired or dead, and fantasy was taking over from science fiction with books about dragons and wizards and their ilk, and that really didn't turn me on.<br /><br />so then, for close to 30 years, i read very little sf at all and i priimarily read what is somewhat ambiguously called literary fiction, even though good genre fiction should be able to be classed as literature, but usually isn't. then, all of a sudden, for reasons that escape me, i started reading sf again recently.and let me digress for a minute. i have never liked the fact that sf stood for science fiction, yet encompassed many books that have no science in them whatsoever. most fantasy novels for example.i think it was harlan ellison,one of my favorite authors, who first suggested that sf should stand for speculative fiction instead. i couldn't agree more as this would cover all of the extremely wide range of books that are lumped under sf.<br /><br /><i>the stars my destination</i> is a shining example of everything that's good about sf. it's a revenge story, it's a love story, it's even kind of a rags to riches story. but above all, it's pretty much non-stop action, with fantastic, memorable characters.<br /><br />it's possible that i may have read this book many years ago, as it was written in 1956, but i don't think so because i'm pretty sure i would have remembered at least some of it.bester really only wrote two novels of consequence, this one and <i>the demolished man</i>, but with these two books he left behind quite a legacy. on the back of this book, robert silverberg says it is "on everybody's list of the ten greatest sf novels". i couldn't agree more, it's an absolute classic. i'm sure that most people who are into sf will have already read this. if not i strongly urge you to do so. immediately. and for any neophytes looking to dip their toe in, this would be a great place to start.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17472495490900707050" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_323754396" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/323754396" />
    <a title="Wanda" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9246169-wanda"><img alt="Wanda" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528903039p2/9246169.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/323754396?book_show_action=true">May 04, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Wanda" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Wanda" href="/user/show/9246169-wanda">Wanda</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9246169-wanda?shelf=speculative-fiction">speculative-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9246169-wanda?shelf=z-1000-guardian">z-1000-guardian</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9246169-wanda?shelf=reading-project">reading-project</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9246169-wanda?shelf=read-in-2016">read-in-2016</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer323754396" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11820488815437741364"><b>You pigs, you. You rut like pigs, is all. You got the most in you, and you use the least. You hear me, you? Got a million in you and spend pennies. Got a genius in you and think crazies. Got a heart in you and feel empties. All a you. Every you...</b><br/><br/>You’d think that something written in the 1950s wouldn’t have too much resonance now, in 2016, wouldn’t you? And yet, <i>The Stars My Destination</i> still speaks to me. Now we have so many advantages. Things like the internet, for example, which is so useful </span>
  <span id="freeText11820488815437741364" style="display:none"><b>You pigs, you. You rut like pigs, is all. You got the most in you, and you use the least. You hear me, you? Got a million in you and spend pennies. Got a genius in you and think crazies. Got a heart in you and feel empties. All a you. Every you...</b><br /><br />You’d think that something written in the 1950s wouldn’t have too much resonance now, in 2016, wouldn’t you? And yet, <i>The Stars My Destination</i> still speaks to me. Now we have so many advantages. Things like the internet, for example, which is so useful and fun. And yet so many people seem to use it only to be nasty and unkind. Got a million in us and spend pennies.<br /><br />I can’t say that I liked the main character, Gully Foyle, but I couldn’t ignore him either. I wanted to know what happened to him. I was pleasantly surprised to realize how many female characters Bester employed, all with substantive roles. I also enjoyed Gully’s vernacular speech, a foreshadowing of novels like <i>A Clockwork Orange</i> or <i>Riddley Walker</i>. <br /><br />Plus, Jaunting (teleportation) seemed to be a great way to completely change society. And yet it changes in completely predictable ways. The wealthy create labyrinths to protect their wealth and their women (for you have to know the co-ordinates of a location to jaunte there). Back to the future, women stuck in the home once more. And still, men with dollar signs in their eyes seem to be in control of things.<br /><br />Who would think that gutter-talking, face-tattooed, criminal Gully would end up being the key to change? Got a genius in him and thinks crazies. Challenging the status quo of money and big corporations running everything.<br /><br />I’ve heard from several people that this novel is like <i>The Count of Monte Cristo</i> in space. That’s inspired me to finally read that famous work in the near future.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="11820488815437741364" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3183485519" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3183485519" />
    <a title="Brent" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3742957-brent"><img alt="Brent" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1501210358p2/3742957.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3183485519?book_show_action=true">Feb 19, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Brent" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Brent" href="/user/show/3742957-brent">Brent</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3742957-brent?shelf=scifi">scifi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3742957-brent?shelf=on-hand">on-hand</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3183485519" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18397401194052233088">So, this book is on several lists of classics, it's the the rough prototype for the Cyberpunk genre, and it's....really, really odd.<br/><br/>It has a surreal, skeletal feel that reminds me of Harlan Ellison, or Philip K. Dick. No subtlety, no subtext, just raw ideas (and characters) blasting off the page and squirming into your brain. <br/><br/>Its great if you like that sort of thing. <br/><br/>If you need more meat and polish, you may want to look elsewhere. </span>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780739435564" href="/book/show/378510.The_Stars_My_Destination">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/131730-rj-from-the-lbc?shelf=guardian-1000-read">guardian-1000-read</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1395515917" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17380396601260026325"><b>"You pigs, you. You rut like pigs, is all. You got the most in you, and you use the least. You hear me, you? Got a million in you and spend pennies. Got a genius in you and think crazies. Got a heart in you and feel empties. All a you. Every you.... I challenge you, me. Die or live and be great. Blow yourselves to Christ gone or come and find me, Gully Foyle, and I make you men. I make you great. I give you the stars."</b><br/><br/>Behold, the birth of cyberpunk. Powerful corporate clans? Check. Cybernetic en</span>
  <span id="freeText17380396601260026325" style="display:none"><b>"You pigs, you. You rut like pigs, is all. You got the most in you, and you use the least. You hear me, you? Got a million in you and spend pennies. Got a genius in you and think crazies. Got a heart in you and feel empties. All a you. Every you.... I challenge you, me. Die or live and be great. Blow yourselves to Christ gone or come and find me, Gully Foyle, and I make you men. I make you great. I give you the stars."</b><br /><br />Behold, the birth of cyberpunk. Powerful corporate clans? Check. Cybernetic enhancements? Check. Strong female leads? Check. Morally ambivalent characters in a noir-ish plot? Check and check. Bester takes all these ideas and jams in a few more, like the mental powers of telepathy and teleportation along with an Atomic-age McGuffin, shakes well, and barfs the result all over the plot of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7126.The_Count_of_Monte_Cristo" title="The Count of Monte Cristo by Alexandre Dumas" rel="nofollow noopener">The Count of Monte Cristo</a>. Yeah, it's raw like that. You hear me, you? I give you the stars. </span>

          </span>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/841700261?book_show_action=true">Dec 02, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Carolyn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Carolyn" href="/user/show/19559507-carolyn">Carolyn</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/11657174-the-stars-my-destination">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19559507-carolyn?shelf=sf">sf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19559507-carolyn?shelf=classic">classic</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer841700261" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6669272222446097253">Gully Foyle, lowest of the low, lazy, crude, murderer, rapist, ignorant brute of a man, hired as a low grade mechanic on the spaceship Nomad. The only survivor of a brutal attack, he scavenged food and oxygen for six months, hiding away in a locker until he sees the spaceship Vorga approach. Finally rescue is at hand, but No, the ship slows, takes a look and then speeds off. Incensed with fury, Foyle swears revenge on the crew of the Vorga. Pulling himself up by his bootstraps he plans his escap</span>
  <span id="freeText6669272222446097253" style="display:none">Gully Foyle, lowest of the low, lazy, crude, murderer, rapist, ignorant brute of a man, hired as a low grade mechanic on the spaceship Nomad. The only survivor of a brutal attack, he scavenged food and oxygen for six months, hiding away in a locker until he sees the spaceship Vorga approach. Finally rescue is at hand, but No, the ship slows, takes a look and then speeds off. Incensed with fury, Foyle swears revenge on the crew of the Vorga. Pulling himself up by his bootstraps he plans his escape and fights tooth and nail to be free to establish himself as an aristocratic self made man as he hunts down the crew and corporations who would leave a man to die in space.<br /><br />This is classic scifi. Published more than 60 years ago it is well written and stands up well in terms of vision and science. Set in the 25th century where everyone has learnt to teleport (jaunt) there is no need for cars, planes or other forms of transport and the world is a very different place. There has never been an anti-hero like Gully Foyle and his actions and choices at the end of the book were astounding. Wonderful stuff!</span>
  <a data-text-id="6669272222446097253" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('9GTwHD0ax3IU2u0VSs5TZ7dokeyzfkor3X+8y85PKpyWAF8u6DUexP0hPLxx7FfM03XEIyY2D1GJnDjwdMO39A==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('Y3/QJaYG+3U6CA1+VmnriMlF5cJFJLADB3xLYpmYr60BG38Xcykiw9Pz3NdtS+8jrViwDdBs9XlTn89ZIxQyxQ==')})
  }

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer9758038802993090353">Alfred Bester was an American science fiction author, TV and radio scriptwriter, magazine editor and scripter for comic strips and comic books. <br/><br/>Though successful in all these fields, he is best remembered for his science fiction, including The Demolished Man, winner of the inaugural Hugo Award in 1953, a story about murder in a future society where the police are telepathic, and The Stars My Desti</span>
  <span id="freeText9758038802993090353" style="display:none">Alfred Bester was an American science fiction author, TV and radio scriptwriter, magazine editor and scripter for comic strips and comic books. <br /><br />Though successful in all these fields, he is best remembered for his science fiction, including The Demolished Man, winner of the inaugural Hugo Award in 1953, a story about murder in a future society where the police are telepathic, and The Stars My Destination, a 1956 SF classic about a man bent on revenge in a world where people can teleport, that inspired numerous authors in the genre and is considered an early precursor to the cyberpunk movement in the 1980s.<br /><br />AKA:<br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/15268644._______________" title="Άλφρεντ Μπέστερ" rel="nofollow noopener">Άλφρεντ Μπέστερ</a> (Greek)</span>
  <a data-text-id="9758038802993090353" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
